<line act="1" scene="1" line="1" speaker="KING HENRY IV">So shaken as we are, so wan with care,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="2" speaker="KING HENRY IV">Find we a time for frighted peace to pant,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="3" speaker="KING HENRY IV">And breathe short-winded accents of new broils</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="4" speaker="KING HENRY IV">To be commenced in strands afar remote.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="5" speaker="KING HENRY IV">No more the thirsty entrance of this soil</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="6" speaker="KING HENRY IV">Shall daub her lips with her own children's blood;</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="7" speaker="KING HENRY IV">Nor more shall trenching war channel her fields,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="8" speaker="KING HENRY IV">Nor bruise her flowerets with the armed hoofs</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="9" speaker="KING HENRY IV">Of hostile paces: those opposed eyes,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="10" speaker="KING HENRY IV">Which, like the meteors of a troubled heaven,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="11" speaker="KING HENRY IV">All of one nature, of one substance bred,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="12" speaker="KING HENRY IV">Did lately meet in the intestine shock</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="13" speaker="KING HENRY IV">And furious close of civil butchery</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="14" speaker="KING HENRY IV">Shall now, in mutual well-beseeming ranks,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="15" speaker="KING HENRY IV">March all one way and be no more opposed</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="16" speaker="KING HENRY IV">Against acquaintance, kindred and allies:</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="17" speaker="KING HENRY IV">The edge of war, like an ill-sheathed knife,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="18" speaker="KING HENRY IV">No more shall cut his master. Therefore, friends,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="19" speaker="KING HENRY IV">As far as to the sepulchre of Christ,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="20" speaker="KING HENRY IV">Whose soldier now, under whose blessed cross</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="21" speaker="KING HENRY IV">We are impressed and engaged to fight,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="22" speaker="KING HENRY IV">Forthwith a power of English shall we levy;</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="23" speaker="KING HENRY IV">Whose arms were moulded in their mothers' womb</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="24" speaker="KING HENRY IV">To chase these pagans in those holy fields</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="25" speaker="KING HENRY IV">Over whose acres walk'd those blessed feet</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="26" speaker="KING HENRY IV">Which fourteen hundred years ago were nail'd</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="27" speaker="KING HENRY IV">For our advantage on the bitter cross.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="28" speaker="KING HENRY IV">But this our purpose now is twelve month old,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="29" speaker="KING HENRY IV">And bootless 'tis to tell you we will go:</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="30" speaker="KING HENRY IV">Therefore we meet not now.
